<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText9749492444076304343" style="display:none">In the seventh book in the bestselling series, evil scientists are still trying to convince Max that she needs to save the world, this time by providing the genetic link in speeding up the pace of evolution. Worse, they're trying to convince her that her perfect mate is Dylan, the newest addition to the flock. The problem is that, despite herself, Max is starting to believe it. <br /><br />Fang travels the country collecting his own gang of evolved humans, but the two separate flocks must unite to defeat a frightening doomsday cult whose motto is Save the Planet: Kill the Humans. And this time, the true heroine, for once, might just be little Angel.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_106651789" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106651789" />
    <a title="Kaela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2988442-kaela"><img alt="Kaela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454476242p2/2988442.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106651789?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaela" href="/user/show/2988442-kaela">Kaela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316036207" href="/book/show/7885091-angel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106651789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8840872196268858683">SPOLIERS. LOTS AND LOTS OF SPOILERS. <br/><br/>*for all reading this, I want you to know that I am an avid, crazy- obsessed max ride fan. its just that this one installment... well, you'll see.I might update this later, when I sound more normal and get the disapointment out of my system.*<br/><br/>and since it's MR, I can't rate it lower than a four. Sorry to all those who agree with the following review. <br/>__________________________________________________________________<br/><br/>Dear James Patterson, <br/><br/>I am willing to forget </span>
  <span id="freeText8840872196268858683" style="display:none">SPOLIERS. LOTS AND LOTS OF SPOILERS. <br /><br />*for all reading this, I want you to know that I am an avid, crazy- obsessed max ride fan. its just that this one installment... well, you'll see.I might update this later, when I sound more normal and get the disapointment out of my system.*<br /><br />and since it's MR, I can't rate it lower than a four. Sorry to all those who agree with the following review. <br />__________________________________________________________________<br /><br />Dear James Patterson, <br /><br />I am willing to forget Maya and Dylan and this 'book' that you published if, in the next one, you bring Max and Fang back together. There are many different types of books that you can pull off a romance switch like that, but Max Ride isn't one. This is where the fandom interrupts your writing, because nearly 90% are team Fang. <br /><br />SO, <br />I suggest that this next and final novel you are writing should end with Max and Fang. This isn't about what you want as an author. You can go and write a side novel just for yourself to satifsy this whole Dylan romance switch feeling. But you are selling these books, and if you want to make money, then you need something people want. Which is FAX. <br /><br />And even though I think you are trying as hard as you can to make it a clean break, I think it would be an insult to all the other books, along with all your fans, to not fix their relationship. At least have them be best friends again. PLEASE. <br />_______________________________________________________________<br /><br />COMPLAINTS:<br /><br />1. <br />QUOTE: <br />"Never, Max," Dylan said. "I'm programmed to imprint on you. You know it. I can't fight the urge to be with you, no matter what."<br />UNQUOTE.<br /><br />JAMES PATTERSON, PLEASE DON'T TELL ME YOU JUST MADE A FREAKING TWILIGHT REFERENCE. <br /><br />2.<br />Mr. Patterson, you must be kidding me...<br />YOU WANT MAX AND DYLAN TO HAVE KIDS? <br />It wouldn't be that bad if it was Fang.<br />BUT DYLAN? <br />AND KIDS? <br /><br />That whole subject in this book disgusts me. It's like it came out of some spaztic teenage girl's messy fanfiction. Its a plot twist that, yes, confused many and was unsuspecting to all readers, but its JUST WRONG. The only good thing that came from that was the jet scene... the only scene where there was a Max/Fang moment that didn't end in, "oh yeah, thats cute, but I'm supposed to hate you so forget it." <br /><br />3. <br />MAYA. JUST NO. NOT COOL. <br /><br />And Dylan should have died after that hypodermic needle incident. just sayin'.<br /><br />______________________________________________________________<br /><br />GOOD PARTS (?)<br />- The plane ride. I already mentioned that, but still, favorite scene. <br />- Angel's alive and has forgotten about the "I rule the world" idea. (but how dare she pick Dylan over Fang!) <br />- That Iggy didn't stay brainwashed. And the Ella thing fell apart. <br />- That Jeb is possibly dead, along with Dr. Gunther Hagen <br />- That there is a *possible* way this book can end that would work for me. (sorry for being so selfish in this review...) <br /><br />There is a way. Since the Fang Gang and the Maxalators didn't completly wipe out the Doomsday Group, then that means in the next book they can do so. And since Max's clone is hangin around, that means that Dylan may have a chance to get a little side tracked.... <br /><br />So brings me to my...<br /><br />conclusion. <br /><br />What could happen? <br /><br />PLAN #1. The world catastrophe ends - either the world is destoryed or they save it. Since this is Maximum Ride and not The Hunger Games, I'm guessing the latter. Maya and Dylan both die, Max + Fang. <br /><br />PLAN #2. No Max + Fang. I burn the book. <br /><br />PLAN #3. Dylan, meet Max's clone, who is a bit nicer and more prone to not hating you. Maya, meet Dylan. And in the back, Max and Fang get back to normal. This, for me, is the best, but it might be a bit too Disney. But then again, so are most of the relationships in this book. <br /><br /><br />Thanks for reading, if you spent the time to listen to my complaining and actually get down this far to read this complaint. I hope that the next (and final, btw) book will finally bring this series to a semi happy close. <br /><br /><br />**EDIT** 4/9/12<br />I tried to reread this. Looking back its way, way worse than I let on before. It is a horrifically written book - guys, my five year old brother could write better than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8840872196268858683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

So that's why I feared for my life in Fang. <br /><br />I think I know what Max would say right about now: "If Fang is in any way harmed - if he gets a <i>hangnail</i> - you won't see another morning."<br /><br />As for the whole Max/Dylan thing, it would depend on if it lasts. <div id="review_190497940" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190497940" />
    <a title="Lyndsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey"><img alt="Lyndsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288890060p2/4224396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190497940?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyndsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyndsey" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey">Lyndsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-4-stars">reviewed-4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=fun-for-the-sake-of-fun">fun-for-the-sake-of-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-mutants">about-mutants</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190497940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18147820179803288414"><b>Also posted on <a href='http://www.STRANGEMORE.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>STRANGEMORE.COM</a>.</b><br/><br/><u>Oh schnikes.</u><br/><br/>James Patterson is now using the word "<i>imprint</i>" now. <b>God help us all.</b><br/><br/>Well, considering the imprinting in this book is from one teenager to another and that they are actually BIRD mutants (the term <i>imprint</i> originated from the act of a baby bird bonding with it's mother), it isn't quite as icky as a wolf imprinting on and falling in instatruelove with a newborn baby. Because we all know that bestiality combined with pedophilia is totally <u>romantic</u>, right? </span>
  <span id="freeText18147820179803288414" style="display:none"><b>Also posted on <a href="http://www.STRANGEMORE.com" rel="nofollow noopener">STRANGEMORE.COM</a>.</b><br><br><u>Oh schnikes.</u><br><br>James Patterson is now using the word "<i>imprint</i>" now. <b>God help us all.</b><br><br>Well, considering the imprinting in this book is from one teenager to another and that they are actually BIRD mutants (the term <i>imprint</i> originated from the act of a baby bird bonding with it's mother), it isn't quite as icky as a wolf imprinting on and falling in instatruelove with a newborn baby. Because we all know that bestiality combined with pedophilia is totally <u>romantic</u>, right? But still, Patterson. WTF?<br><br>Other than the obvious blatant attempt to appeal to the Twilight generation with the onset of a love triangle between a blond Adonis-type mutant and the rugged dark-haired broody mutant, I had a lot of fun reading this book and the series in general.<br><br>I probably should be ashamed to say that I read the Maximum Ride series, but who am I kidding? <u>I have no shame.</u> It's a guilty pleasure. I started reading them before I matured literaturicly, and no, I'm not sure that I'm proving my point by using a made up word like <i>literaturicly</i> but "So what? Who cares?" *multiple exaggerated shoulder shrugs*<br><br><u>
  <b>The Rundown</b>
</u><br><br>For you sci-fi gurus, you may notice similarities with James Cameron's masterpiece television series <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00005JLJM/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=findthebook-20&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;camp=217145&amp;creative=399373&amp;creativeASIN=B00005JLJM" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Angel</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380354699i/707387.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">, which if you haven't watched... what the hell is wrong with you? Let me break it down: Jessica Alba, as a mutant, kicking ass while wearing leather - <i>Do you need more convincing than that? REALLY?!</i><br><br>Some facts about the Maximum Ride series by James Patterson:<br><br>	* Girl named Max, short for Maximum.<br>	* She kicks ass and doesn't stop to take names.<br>	* She is a mutant with special abilities because of her recombinant DNA.<br>	* She has a "flock" of other friends with special abilities.<br>	* Her love interest is part of her group but it seems they are destined to NOT be together.<br>	* Her main job is saving the world, but she mostly ends up just doing a few odd jobs here and there.<br><br>While this may not be Dawson's Creek with mutant teens who have a ridiculously large vocabulary, it IS a lot like Dark Angel, complete with angst, wangst, and a love triangle but specifically with recombinant DNA bird kids! WOOOOOO!<br><br>These books are by no means "brain food." In fact, most would consider them juvenile, which is one thing I love about them. They don't use complex or lyrical language. They can be melodramatic at times, but mostly they are just unadulterated fun, not to mention entirely addictive.<br><br><u>
  <b>The Tone and Pacing</b>
</u><br><br>The Maximum Ride books usually fly at a breakneck speed and don't often slow down. The flock is always on the move, always performing ridiculous feats of awesomeness, and always making stupid jokes. Regardless of the camp in these books, they have a lot of heart also, as well as great messages for younger teens or pre-teens.<br><br><i>"There's nothing more dangerous than someone trying to act for the greater good."</i><br><br>Which is so true in lots of ways. Many horrific things have been done in the name of the greater good. Hitler thought the Holocaust would create a superior master race. Religious extremist think that ridding the world of all religious opposition is for the greater good. People who think they have the best intentions can often be the most <u>ruthless</u>.<br><br>Apart from messages about saving the world and being the best version of yourself, there are also not-so-complex undertones about doing what's right and taking care of the planet. It did get a little preachy for my taste in one or two of the books, but overall, the series is still worthwhile and hella fun to read. And there is only ONE more after this book. *cries like a little baby, like a little baby in it's crib*<br><br><u>
  <b>The Verdict</b>
</u><br><br>I'm so ridiculously attached to these books and these characters that I just can't give this one any less than 4 stars.<br><br>There are not very many articulate reviews of these books (I mean one review actually calls a main character "butt poop") and unfortunately the books themselves are not highly intelligent. There aren't really any prerequisites here. <u>No thinking required.</u><br><br>The Scarecrow could read these books. *sings* "If I only had <i>intelligent conversational techniques</i>."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380354699i/707388.jpg" width="163" height="240" alt="SCARECROW" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>These books are FUN, FUN, FUN! And mainly just that, which is exactly what I needed.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18147820179803288414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And I hear there will be yet ANOTHER book coming out after this. <br/>I LOVE Maximum Ride, but seriously, even good things have to come to an end.   <span id="freeText1961256896279805487" style="display:none">This series should have ended three books ago, before all that stupid global warming stuff. And I hear there will be yet ANOTHER book coming out after this. <br />I LOVE Maximum Ride, but seriously, even good things have to come to an end. And if this ends up like all the other series I read that went on too long, the series is only gonna get worse. From what I've read of Angel, that's the way it's going to be.<br /><br />I mean, issues:<br /><br />-Dylan. Ewwwww. Just, no.<br />-Fang leaves. News flash James Patterson. Fang is one of the ONLY reasons people read Maximum Ride. In fact, I think it should be called Fang, not Maximum Ride.<br />-Angel. I get that Max still sees her as a little, well, angel, but she ISN'T! She is a backstabbing trouble maker with an ironic name.<br />-The Voice. Ignoring the fact that the idea of a Voice is stupid, the voice is a hipocrite. "Fang is your soulmate." So Max listens to the Voice, and dates him. Then the Voice is like "Dylan is your perfect other half." Would the Voice just make up his (her?) mind?<br />-Iggy. Gazzy. Nudge. Iggy again(cause I love him). So, when did these characters become, like, non-exsistant? They havn't done anything substantial in a while.<br />-Plot. Find one.<br /><br />There's more, but I'm too lasy to type it. But I think I'm alowed to be too lasy to type the issues if James Patterson is too lazy to fix them.<br />All I can say is that I hope I'm not wasting my money on yet another dissapointing sequel.<br /><br />AFTER READING:<br /><br />Worst. Max. Ride. Book. Ever.<br /><br />You could tell just by they way he ended it in a cliff hanger that he didn't know how many people would buy it.<br /><br />One thing about people is they change, but I can guarentee that no one does so much so fast. Fang. Max. Angel. They are COMPLETELY DIFFERENT PEOPLE!!!!<br /><br />And let's also point who was in, maybe, 5 chapters in the book.<br />-Iggy<br />-Nudge<br />-Jeb<br />-Ella<br />-Dr. Martinez<br />-Voice<br />-Akila<br />-Total<br />-Gazzy<br /><br />The "Fang Gang" nobodys that we don't care about got more mention than really anyone above.<br /><br />I believe that JP is forgeting who is in his books, and what powers they had, because, no one really used their powers eccept for the Fang Gang.<br /><br />And worst of all<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br /><br />Sorry. Spoilers ahead, so I hid them with arrows. Just scroll down to see it.<br /><br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br />\/<br /><br /><br />FANG BECAME A JERK!!!!!!!!!!!!! :_(<br /><br />yeah. i know. suckish and it ruined the whole thing. "Maya" (Max II) is stupid and how could he just replace Max with her?</span>

They HAVE to get together! :3" Then reading Max, "Oh, YES! Finally! :D" Come Fang, and here's what I thought. "-___- Oh, please." <br /><br />Last time I checked, the Flock was on the run, kicking Eraser butt. Then the ever so wonderful JP (Erhem!) goes and gets rid of the Erasers waaaay too abruptly. It made me happy that the Flock could relax and such, but after a whole book of NOTHING, I was tired of it. (Bahaha, I never thought Max would think like that.) Angel is BIPOLAR. Jeb is still a WEIRDO. I've never almost pucked because of a book until NOW. I'm gonna read this book, even if it KILLS ME!<br /><br /><br />That's it. Of course I'm reading it. As puke worthy as the idea is, we all wanna know how Max deals with this... "Breeding thingy."<br /><br />Yup. <br /><br />...?<br /><br />Blargh.<br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130338272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6779648187646470098">(sad sigh)<br/>You know how some books make you squeal in delight once you buy them, even if you know bad things are going to happen in that book? You just have to be happy, because you love the series and the characters and you know it'll all be alright, even if you also have an inkling that some of the main characters are going to die?<br/>Yeah. I don't feel that anymore for this series.<br/>The first three books, they were great. The series could have--and maybe should have--ended there. And why? Because th</span>
  <span id="freeText6779648187646470098" style="display:none">(sad sigh)<br />You know how some books make you squeal in delight once you buy them, even if you know bad things are going to happen in that book? You just have to be happy, because you love the series and the characters and you know it'll all be alright, even if you also have an inkling that some of the main characters are going to die?<br />Yeah. I don't feel that anymore for this series.<br />The first three books, they were great. The series could have--and maybe should have--ended there. And why? Because the enemy was the School. They were a believable foe, someone you know you hate but are glad for, in a way, because they'll always be there to rip your guts open. Now, though, I have honestly no idea who the enemy is anymore. (Well, I know Angel is an antagonist. I mean, she's betrayed the flock time after time, and they're all gullible enough to take her back, just waiting to see what evil thing she'll do next.) Anyway, the enemy was global warming, I think. Then it was Mr. Chu. Then it was the guy who created Dylan. Now it's, I don't know, people who want to kill the human race, and for good reason I might add. You don't know if Jeb is good or evil, although if you look at his personality, he may care for Max, but he's evil to the core. <br />I wish I could get all my frustrations out but it's kind of wordless, ya know? There's only one more thing I have to say: Mr. Patterson, let the series come to an end. The books are fine, but the characters are...well, not. RIP Maximum RIde. <br /><br />Oh, and that whole "Save the planet: Kill the humans" thing sounds a lot like what Jeb's group of evil cohorts tried to do with the half and half plan or whatever it's called.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4245941810257914699">I freakin' NEED this book! My life depends on it! Well, not really, but I'm obsessed with the Maximum Ride series and I don't know if I can wait till next year!<br/><br/>Update:<br/><br/>Finally! Finally I have this book in my hands! Now, let's see if it lives up to the Maximum Ride name.<br/><br/>Yet again...another update:<br/><br/>I just finished this book today and, to my surprise, I really liked it.   <span id="freeText4245941810257914699" style="display:none">I freakin' NEED this book! My life depends on it! Well, not really, but I'm obsessed with the Maximum Ride series and I don't know if I can wait till next year!<br /><br />Update:<br /><br />Finally! Finally I have this book in my hands! Now, let's see if it lives up to the Maximum Ride name.<br /><br />Yet again...another update:<br /><br />I just finished this book today and, to my surprise, I really liked it. I mean, I totally ship FAX, but I wouldn't mind it if Max and Dylan got together. I'm still kinda angry at Fang for leaving Max in the first place (I know, I know, he's not real, but STILL!). Also, I like the fact that in this book there is an ACTUAL bad guy! Max isn't chasing after some vague "save the world" nonsense. They actually have to stop an evil organization from destroying the world! And to that I say, HALLELUJAH!!! I was really starting to doubt James Patterson's ability to come up with antagonists. The closest thing Max had to one was the School and that hasn't been around since, like, the third book.<br />Anyway, enough of my ranting, I really enjoyed this book. I think it's going to be one of my favorites. Not because of the fighting or the romance, but because Max really matured throughout this book. She showed another side of her personality. Instead of being tough and emotionless all of the time, she showed a more vulnerable side. And I think that gave her more depth as a character, in my opinion anyway.</span>

  <span id="freeText3267109617324722498" style="display:none">A note on Max and Dylan/Max and Fang...<br /><br />Okay, James Patterson, MAKE UP YOUR MIND ALREADY. Is Max gonna be with Fang or with Dylan? Personally, I would PREFER (Note: Prefer meaning, I would be eternally happy if you did it, and burn all the books if you didn't) if Max and Fang are together, but, hey, it's your call. Please, make the right one. The only MAJORLY annoying thing about romance in this book, was the Dylan/Fang thing. So, is Max like "Oh, well, since Fang's gone, I guess I should just like Dylan now, right?" and Fang's basically like "Max is gone. Boohoo. I'll just hang out and do my own thing now." Ugh, I mean, really? Max and Fang DESERVE to be together, I think that's, like, a mutual decision between all readers. Dylan stinks, Fang Forever. James Patterson, if you're reading this, PLEASE don't have Max get together with that newbie hunka-junka. Fang has been around since the first flippin' book, and Max and Fang LOVE each other. Dylan is "imprinted" with Max, but that doesn't mean she is imprinted with him! She should go with Fang. Fang likes her. She likes Fang. It works. Dylan can hook up with Max II. It's settled. Cuz, ya know, I don't know about anybody ELSE, but I think that Dylan is a little...new. Max hardly KNOWS him. She knows Fang like the back of her hand. It's not that complicated, guys.<br /><br />A note on Angel...<br /><br />I loved, loved, loved, loved, loved Angel in this book!!!!!!!!!!! ...let's backtrack a bit. So, I LOVED Angel in the first book, thought she was still pretty cool in the second book, started to think she was a little creepy in the third, disliked her in the fourth book, HATED her in the fifth book, but, James Patterson, did you resurrect an epic character or what? Now she's, like, all "Max, do what YOU think!! I believe in you!" stuff instead of "Max, I should be the leader! Not YOU!". I like her this way. Of course, I sobbed my head off when she supposedly died then went "Oh, WHEW" when I realized she wasn't actually dead. THANK YOU JAMES FOR NOT KILLING A AWESOME-THEN-EVIL-THEN-AWESOME CHARACTER!!!!!!<br /><br />A Note on Fang's Gang...<br /><br />Remind me again, what was the point of Fang leaving? So Max could hook up with Dylan?? So Fang could start his little club? Fang's Gang was probably my least favorite part of the book. They were all arguing at one point and then they seemed pretty invincible at other times. It was a bit of a stretch on James Patterson's part, and I didn't really like it. And the whole "replace Max with Max II" was stupid. I mean, really, Fang? Go away from Max then expect her to give you a warm welcome when you come back when you've been chillin' with her clone? Plus a bunch of other honkidy-donks? Ratchet was fine, Star and Kate were annoying, Holden was weird with his Starfish stuff, Max II (or should I say Maya?) was downright OBNOXIOUS. Argh. Then, of course, Fang gets all angry at Max because she likes Dylan...I mean, dude, seriously, you LEFT HER. That doesn't mean that I like Dylan, cuz I hate 'im, it just means that Fang is being a little hypocritical towards Max...dontcha think? <br /><br />A Note on Iggy...<br /><br />To all those fans who kept saying "It's Iggy's Turn!" and "the book should be named IGGY! Not ANGEL!", well, unless you wanted an entire book devoted to Iggy being in the looney bin believing in the one light (which was sorta the only major role he played)? Think about it. It would've been a short, and BORING book. Face it. It WAS Angel's turn. Course, hopefully the next one will be named GAZZY, but I doubt it. Oh, and the entire Iggy + Ella thingy was SOOO cute! :) I never expected them to like each other, and when they were all cosy-cosy it was, honestly, quite adorable. Call me easily persuaded, but I think that they should be together. James Patterson, please, listen too all this stuff, 'mkay?<br /><br />A Note on Gazzy...<br /><br />*Sniffle* I feel bad for the poor kid. He's my #1 favorite character (Well, he and Max are tied), and I wish he could've disabled those bombs. He had it in him. He's still epic, though. REALLY epic. But, another thing, he like "didn't save Jeb", remember? So, what, is this James Patterson's "Let's make Gazzy look bad" book? It's okay, man, but, please, give the kid a break.<br /><br />A note on Dylan...<br /><br />Jeez, dude, seriously. I wish Dylan would REALIZE THAT MAX LIKES FANG AND VICE VERSA. Why can't he un-imprint Max? Why??? He's a newbie and seemingly invincible. Max deserves somebody that's, *cough*, MILDLY normal, know what I mean? And, Max is supposed to be Miss My-Way, and she seems to be falling a little bit to Dylan against her will...anybody else notice the dramatic change? It might just be Fang leaving, or it might just be Dylan's secret evil mind controlling powers that we'll learn about in book 8, because Dylan is actually helping Dr. Gunther Hagen...which reminds me of the next thing I need to mention...<br /><br />A note on Max's Mom, Jeb and Dr. Gunther Hagen...<br /><br />What happened to THEM? They were there at the begginning, then POOF. Gone. Whoosh. Forgotten. I hope they find them in the next book. Oh, and Ella too! Let's find Ella too. Don't forget about that. That would be bad, JP. VERY bad. VERY, VERY, VERY bad.<br /><br /><br />On a whole, this was an AMAZING book. Though my review probably sounds a bit negative... Whatever. I LOVED this book, and it was DEFINITELY one of the better ones in the series (i.e. Better than Final Warning). Call me biased towards books where Max and Fang are together, but ANGEL was NOT as good as FANG, or MAX, but it was REALLY close. I can't wait for the last book!!!!<br /><br />Did anybody else notice how James Patterson said that the last Max Ride book would be released in February of 2012? 2012??? That's the supposed "end of the world" year, right?<br /><br />I hope he's not implying something, there...<br /><br />Maybe it just takes him a year to write a book...<br /><br />-Ruthie the #1 Max Ride fan!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3267109617324722498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5020501827908200933" style="display:none">Angel - Continuing the Twilightification of The Maximum Ride Series or saving it from a fate worse then death? SPOILERS!<br /><br /><br />First, Uh, Angel it's Iggy's turn to have the spotlight. :/ Poor Iggy, it looks as if he's been pushed to the side in the Max Ride novels. He had the potential to be such a great character too...<br /><br /><br />Secondy, JP, I honestly hope this book is better the past three. Everything after the third book has just been so... Bland. I've been so disappointed with the direction these books have been taking. <br /><br /><br />First the message "SAVE THE WORLD AND GO GREEN." was stuck upon these books like some company paid JP to add the message to the books or something. With book 5, Fang, the Maximum Ride series begun falling into the dark depths of the Twilight universe, perhaps to never return.<br /><br /><br />I can see Mr Patterson is attempting to leap onto the Twilight bandwagon, like every freaking other new teen release out there. Max is meant to be with FANG. Not Dylan. This was established in the first books. <br /><br /><br />Dylan is a hastily constructed too-attractive boy meant to suck Max into the pointless love triangle that lovesick middle schoolers and rabid Twi-hards fantasize about.<br /><br /><br />I hope Angel will turn things around and bring back the brilliant world of Maximum Ride that I fell in love with back in books 1 - 3, because Maximum Ride was once my favorite series of all time. :(<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_150842437" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150842437" />
    <a title="Fairelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5044454-fairelle"><img alt="Fairelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298781165p2/5044454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150842437?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fairelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fairelle" href="/user/show/5044454-fairelle">Fairelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150842437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15712341475631995904">I recently read Angel and Fang, and I have like a billion complaints. I'm actually disappointed for the most part considering this is one of my favorite book series ever. I loved the humor and the characters (before book #6) .The plot is getting a bit messy and it's pretty unorganized. I'm not sure if it was bad or good.<br/>WARNING, POSSIBLE SPOILERS:<br/><br/>I feel as if I have to put Max first.<br/>Max: Please, JP, I'm begging you, get rid of her mushy mushy-ness. I used to love Max, she was so bad ass and funn</span>
  <span id="freeText15712341475631995904" style="display:none">I recently read Angel and Fang, and I have like a billion complaints. I'm actually disappointed for the most part considering this is one of my favorite book series ever. I loved the humor and the characters (before book #6) .The plot is getting a bit messy and it's pretty unorganized. I'm not sure if it was bad or good.<br />WARNING, POSSIBLE SPOILERS:<br /><br />I feel as if I have to put Max first.<br />Max: Please, JP, I'm begging you, get rid of her mushy mushy-ness. I used to love Max, she was so bad ass and funny and cool. Now she's sitting in a tree wallowing in self pity. A girl who had nothing, who was raised in a lab, has been kicking ass her whole life, should NOT be crying in a tree in self pity. I even dislike her now somewhat. The only reason it's only somewhat is because I become unusually attached to protagonists. I have an affinity towards them.<br /><br />I miss Ari. He actually had reasons to do things, he actually had some depth. His death was really sad. I'm not going to lie, a few tears threatened to spill over when Max was reading Fang's departing letter, but I feel losing a brother forever is sadder than your boyfriend leaving you.<br /><br />What's up with the Voice? First he's like, "Fang is your soul mate! HOORAY!" and now he's egging on all the Dylan crap. ...EH?<br /><br />Erasers: They were soooo awesome. I miss them too :(<br /><br />What happened to the entire School thing? That was one of the coolest things about Maximum Ride, and their determination to defeat the School.<br />Now that they have, I don't know what to say.<br /><br />Dylan? He is a shallow character, he has no depth, no importance, he is not a character that demands interest from me. "Mr. Perfect" is just a Mary Sue that has done nothing remarkable. If he and Max have kids, I have given up all hope for James Patterson. Who sings to get people to stop fighting? WTH? He is abusive towards Max. It looks like he's trying to beat her up in the first part. Why didn't his suicide work? *bursts into sobs*<br /><br />Maya. I also hate Maya. She barely has any depth either. <br /><br />Angel. Okay; I really, really like the old Angel. I completely hated her in Fang. I'm not into on/off characters that stab your back every time you turn around. I honestly wouldn't be too upset if she died. I have pretty mixed feelings for her atm.<br /><br />Fang: JP ARE YOU AN IDIOT OF EPIC PORPORTIONS OR ARE YOU JUST... Fans eat up all the Fax stuff. They are a much better couple than Dylan and Max will ever be. Though, now I personally think Max should just dump both their asses and fly off.<br /><br />Nudge, Izzy and Gazzy: NEED MORE SCREENTIME. They are awesome, and they should keep doing what they are doing because I have none to minor complaints about their characters. I think the only time I laughed in this book was when Iggy was posing as an angel. <br /><br />Why is the book called Angel? The only part revolving around Angel was the last parts. The true heroine is not Angel. The series is called Maximum Ride. Has she even done anything except irritate people?<br /><br />I am obviously going to read the last book because I am stubborn. If I was not stubborn I would have given up the Korean manhwa "Love in the Mask" the second Ji-Woong came in (btw, don't read it, the story has become increasingly stupid) and I just want to see the ending and get it over with.<br /><br />I don't know, if you ask me, "Saving the World and Other Extreme Sports" was the funniest, the best, and the most well-written installation of the Maximum Ride series.<br /><br />Right now I'm just going to have to believe JP planned all this as to get a bigger reaction when the last book becomes hilarious and awesome again. Atleast that's what I'm telling myself to stop my urges to destroy the book. Though I give JP sexy points for including manga and anime in the book. <s>We otaku WILL rule the world!</s><br /> <br />I didn't read book four yet, btw. But I read all the others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15712341475631995904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iyXEa+PY4jO+NrfjlCrVGlsUqoikhaSLiJgP7EBfe3GxA625WIYrWxkdA4Jj39/FjUtNQGoIKuzT5kldjRyJ6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j13dTPBIamNTkwxeA3rlADBs7+yE1851BPMl8aY/XP+1e7SeSxajC/S4uD/0j+/f5jMIJEpaQBJfjWNAa3yuZQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7603300071880332126"><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official US Site</a><br/><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official UK Site</a><br/><a href='http://jimmypatterson.org' rel='nofollow noopener'>JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br/><a href='http://readkiddoread.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadKiddoRead</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText7603300071880332126" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>
